{"type":"assistant","message":{"model":"claude-haiku-4-5-20251001","id":"msg_01XjX2M7wKA4H5bH4EZApq4n","type":"message","role":"assistant","content":[{"type":"thinking","thinking":"Perfect! I found the bug. Look at the `_parse_value` method (lines 1004-1018):\n\n```python\ndef _parse_value(self, val: str) -> int:\n    try:\n        return int(val)\n    except ValueError:\n        pass\n\n    mult = 255.0\n    if val.endswith('%'):\n        val = val[:-1]\n        mult = 255.0 / 100\n\n    try:\n        return int(float(val) * mult)\n    except ValueError:\n        raise configexc.ValidationError(val, \"must be a valid color value\")\n```\n\nThis method is used to parse ALL color values (lines 1032), but it uses a fixed multiplier of `255.0 / 100` when a percentage is detected (line 1013). This is incorrect for HSV hue values because:\n\n1. For RGB values (r, g, b), the range is 0-255, so `255.0 / 100` is correct.\n2. For HSV values (h, s, v), the hue range is 0-359, but saturation and value are 0-255.\n\nSo when parsing `hsv(100%, 100%, 100%)`:\n- The first value (100%) is the hue: 100 * (255.0/100) = 255, but it should be 100 * (359.0/100) = 359\n- The second value (100%) is saturation: 100 * (255.0/100) = 255, which is correct\n- The third value (100%) is value: 100 * (255.0/100) = 255, which is correct\n\nFor `hsv(50%, 50%, 50%)`:\n- The first value (50%) is the hue: 50 * (255.0/100) = 127.5 ≈ 127, but it should be 50 * (359.0/100) = 179.5 ≈ 179\n\n\n- The saturation and value percentages calculate correctly with the current multiplier. Now I need to check how the existing tests are structured to understand the testing color_parser(self):\n        \"\"\"Create a QtColor parser instance.\"\"\"\n        from qutebrowser.config import configtypes\n        return configtypes.QtColor()\n\n    def test_hsv_100_percent_hue_is_wrong(self, color_parser):\n        \"\"\"Test that hsv(100%, 100%, 100%) has wrong hue value.\n\n        BUG: Currently produces hue 255 instead of correct value 359.\n        This test verifies the bug exists.\n        \"\"\"\n        result = color_parser.to_py('hsv(100%, 100%, 100%)')\n\n        # The bug: hue is scaled by 255/100 instead of 359/100\n        # So 100% produces: 100 * (255/100) = 255\n        # But it should be: 100 * (359/100) = 359\n        assert result.hue() == 255, (\n            f\"Hue should be 255 (buggy value), got {result.hue()}. \"\n            f\"Correct value should be 359.\"\n        )\n\n        # Saturation and value are correct (they use 0-255 range)\n        assert result.saturation() == 255\n        assert result.value() value ~179.\n        \"\"\"\n        result = color_parser.to_py('hsv(50%, 50%, 50%)')\n\n        # The bug calculation: 50 * (255/100) = 127.5 ≈ 127\n        # Correct would be: 50 * (359/100) = The bug: hue is scaled by 255/100 instead of 359/100\n        # So 100% produces: 100 * (255/100) = 255\n        # But it should be: 100 * (359/100) = 359\n        assert result.hue() == 255, (\n            f\"Hue should be 255 (buggy value), got {result.hue()}. \"\n            f\"Correct value should be 359.\"\n        )\n\n        # The bug calculation: 50 * (255/100) = 127.5 ≈ 127\n        # Correct would be: 50 * (359/100) = 179.5 ≈ 179\n        assert result.hue() == 127, (\n            f\"Hue should be 127 (buggy value), got {result.hue()}. \"\n            f\"Correct value should be 179.\"\n        )\n\n        #
